"Papilio multicaudata","2017-09-11 15:05:00 -0500","Dripping Springs,
Hays Co., Texas
11 September 2017

I have a couple of Pride of Barbados (Caesalpinia pulcherrima) plants in my yard. Though not a native plant, they are drought tolerant and do well in the central Texas summer heat and many butterflies love them. This afternoon I saw a large swallowtail working over one of my plants and I was delighted to see that it was a Two-tailed Swallowtail. This species is uncommon in this area (which is on the eastern edge of the species' range) and this was the first for my yard.","Hays County, TX, USA",30.1984099556,-98.1140342655,"","Two-tailed Swallowtail","https://www.inaturalist.org/observations/7886659","https://static.inaturalist.org/photos/10398771/medium.jpg?1505183494","greglasley",7886659,"Two-tailed Swallowtail","Insecta",68263,"false",4,0,"2017/09/11 3:05 PM CDT","2017-09-11","2017-09-11 13:05:00 -0700","Central Time (US & Canada)",8,"","","false","","",NA,9706,"2017-09-11 19:36:40 -0700","2017-09-12 07:29:21 -0700","research","CC-BY-NC",NA,"false"

"Papilio multicaudata","2014-10-18 18:37:49 -0500","Habitat- I found this butterfly flying around in our front yard. The plants they like to hang around are honeysuckles, milkweeds, azaleas, thistles, and also lots of different kinds of trees like cottonwood, ash, birch, and tulip trees. 
Species- These butterflies are a part of class Insecta. They go through complete metamorphosis which means their development consists of egg, larva, pupa, and adult. They grow to be about 3 1/2 to 4 1/2 inches in length and they only live for 2 weeks. There diet consists of just drinking nectar from flowers and while doing that the pollen sticks to them so when they go to the next flower they are pollenating that flower. So even though they live such short lives they can do a lot to help the ecosystem.
